  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c19e4432-a83e-488b-925a-f75c0cd1cf9c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

A random moment, his window to her world, and yet it had pierced his excuse for a soul as if it were destiny. As if she were his destiny.         <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101479162" href="/book/show/10211192-falling-under">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5771244-sabrina?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204459641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer886359356602647854">I have to admit: sometimes (often) I pick up books just because I like the cover art. This one in particular reminded me of <i>
  <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Beauty_(film)' rel='nofollow noopener'>American Beauty</a>
</i>, so I couldn't resist.<br/><br/><b>ALERT: this is going to be bitchy.</b><br/><br/><b>I threw this book before even finishing the first chapter.</b><br/>Why?<br/>Because I've already cringed my teeth four times in the first three pages. And that's too much.<br/><br/>I'm going to show you what I mean.<br/><br/>The protagonist is on the bed, reading from her iPhone. And she speaks about her love for books:<blockquote>Every night I</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText886359356602647854" style="display:none">I have to admit: sometimes (often) I pick up books just because I like the cover art. This one in particular reminded me of <i>
  <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Beauty_(film)" rel="nofollow noopener">American Beauty</a>
</i>, so I couldn't resist.<br /><br /><b>ALERT: this is going to be bitchy.</b><br /><br /><b>I threw this book before even finishing the first chapter.</b><br />Why?<br />Because I've already cringed my teeth four times in the first three pages. And that's too much.<br /><br />I'm going to show you what I mean.<br /><br />The protagonist is on the bed, reading from her iPhone. And she speaks about her love for books:<blockquote>Every night I went somewhere new and pretended to be someone else—someone interesting—[…]<br />But the burning man falling from the sky pulled me from my faraway world.</blockquote>You don't say. Really?<br />Here I was depicting in my head this dumb chick, daydreaming on her bed with a vacuous expression on her face, when a burning man falls from the sky screaming his head off, and she just turns her head and says vapidly "Oh, a burning man falling from the sky."<br />Maybe that's not the image the author wanted to give, but it's what she delivered.<br /><br /><blockquote>He was more than <i>on</i> fire. He <i>was</i> fire.</blockquote>And what's the difference? Bho, the author doesn't tell. To me, he looked just like a man on fire.<br /><br /><blockquote>(...) but it was his eyes that caused me to suck in my breath</blockquote>Ok. Reality check here: 1. he's burning; 2. he's falling from the sky; 3. you are looking at him through a window; 4. you are on the bed, supposedly at some distance from said window. How the fuck can you discern something about his eyes!?<br /><br /><blockquote>I leaned farther into the window, the glass surprisingly warm from his brush past it.</blockquote>Do you know what it takes to warm a pane of glass at a distance, say to increase it of 1°C (and you can't even perceive so small an increase)? It takes a fucking lot. Not just some miserable guy on fire falling from the sky and incidentally passing near the window for two seconds. If you haven't the common sense to guess that, do your research.<br /><br />When the man is fallen, she goes near him to help (but without actually doing something helpful). There is a short and improbable dialogue, and then:<blockquote>He rattled and spoke his last words. “Worth … the … fall.”</blockquote>Oh, because she is so beautiful and <i>speshul</i> that it was worth it to fucking be set on fire and be thrown from who knows what highness to precipitate on her fucking garden.<br />What. The. Fuck.<br /><br />I don't want to see this kind of <s>book</s> crap, ever again.<br />I should put this on my "blacklist of bad books", but I pride myself on being honest and I can't honestly give an informed judgment about the book, because I haven't read it. I just can't. So I'm going to put this among my give-ups and you will have to make up your own mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="886359356602647854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_123352002" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123352002" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572125481p2/3283298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123352002?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=24-ebooks">24-ebooks</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123352002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15323760372211697638">Favorite quote: Theia to Haden whilst alone in her bedroom: <i>"Do you know I have never seen a penis?"</i> <br/><br/>ROFL XD Way to go girl, way to go...<br/><br/>If I had to pick a serious quote as my favorite it would probably be this one, though: <br/><br/><i>"This isn't a crush; it's obsession. You are never not in my thoughts. Your scent carries across a room and paralyzes me with longing. I don't want to hold your hand. Part of me wants to set you on fire and hold you while the flame consumes us both, to eat your heart so I kno</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15323760372211697638" style="display:none">Favorite quote: Theia to Haden whilst alone in her bedroom: <i>"Do you know I have never seen a penis?"</i> <br /><br />ROFL XD Way to go girl, way to go...<br /><br />If I had to pick a serious quote as my favorite it would probably be this one, though: <br /><br /><i>"This isn't a crush; it's obsession. You are never not in my thoughts. Your scent carries across a room and paralyzes me with longing. I don't want to hold your hand. Part of me wants to set you on fire and hold you while the flame consumes us both, to eat your heart so I know that only I possess it entirely"</i> <br /><br />Well...at least he’s honest O_o<br /><br />When I started reading Falling Under I got quickly bothered by how the story seemed to follow all the typical paranormal YA clichés. Unbelievably hot guy comes to town, unbelievably insecure and shy heroine gets paired with him for a school project, hot guy tells heroine that she needs to stay away from him for her own safety, heroine goes to some kind of fortune teller who of course tells her that she’s in grave danger, because obviously there’s something evil after her. (Now who could that be??) and so on...Granted, Hayes put these clichés to use with a wink and the digs at Twilight were funny, but still; the attempts to mock her own usage of clichés didn’t really make it any less annoying. But all of that would have been excusable IMO if she had made the romance somewhat unique but unfortunately, this was not the case. It was the same old OMG-I-love-you-and-I’m-going-to-sacrifice-my-soul-for-you-even-though-I’ve-only-known-you-for-a-week and I’m so sick of this kind of romance.<br /><br />What I really, really liked though, was the explanation for it all. What Haden really is and why they can’t be together...now this was something to make this book stand out against all the others but unfortunately I can’t tell you about it since it would be a major spoiler. It’s a pity, I think if Hayes had done the romance part differently this story would’ve had the potential to be really great and different. I also liked how Hayes managed to keep me on my toes. Several times I was surprised, if not shocked, by the turn of events or how the story took on a very creepy note all of the sudden.<br /><br />Altogether I can say that I enjoyed this and I’m pretty sure that some of my friends (like Tina, Nic or Amber for example) will have a blast with this one since they’re known to be a bit more forgiving when it comes to the kind of romance I mentioned. :)<br /></span>

<div id="review_169543074" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169543074" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169543074?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-demons">pn-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=paranormal-general">paranormal-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2011-publication">2011-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=boys-who-are-jerks">boys-who-are-jerks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=mythic-and-fairy-tale-ish">mythic-and-fairy-tale-ish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-succubus">pn-succubus</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169543074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer766260603515273826">I have wildly mixed feelings about this book, which is loosely based on the myth of Persephone. I'm not sure I can write a coherent review because I'm so conflicted, so here goes the pros and cons list.<br/><br/><b>For the first two thirds of the book:</b><br/><br/>* I was pretty annoyed with the main character Theia. Stop falling in love with boys just because they're kinda cute, girls! <br/>* I really, really disliked Haden. Manipulative, bad-tempered, controlling, stalker-ish guys who try to make girls jealous, especially w</span>
  <span id="freeText766260603515273826" style="display:none">I have wildly mixed feelings about this book, which is loosely based on the myth of Persephone. I'm not sure I can write a coherent review because I'm so conflicted, so here goes the pros and cons list.<br /><br /><b>For the first two thirds of the book:</b><br /><br />* I was pretty annoyed with the main character Theia. Stop falling in love with boys just because they're kinda cute, girls! <br />* I really, really disliked Haden. Manipulative, bad-tempered, controlling, stalker-ish guys who try to make girls jealous, especially while <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[grinding their hips against other girls during a dance while eye-locked with the main character <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, make me want to resort to violence.<br /><br /><i>I can't get a handle on the guy. Sometimes he seems so into you, and other times he's...sort of the Antichrist.</i> Exactly!<br /><br />* I saw no reason for Theia's dialogue to be so stilted. I understand why Haden's was, but speaking with a British accent doesn't mean she has to talk as if she's straight out of some boring 18th century period drama. Even her father's dialogue was less formal than hers.<br />* I got a little tired of all the "Touch me!" "But I can't..." "I want you to!" "You'll die!" "But it's sooo worth it!" drama that kept repeating over and over.<br />* I really didn't buy into the mix of attractive boy/dangerous "man" thing.<br />* I wasn't sure why Haden was so attracted to Theia at first...how many boys are enthralled by spying on a girl playing the violin? Although I did really like the way Theia's hair was described, all gold and caramel curls. Lovely!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>However...</i>
</b><br /><br />* The opening is pretty darned good. Burning man falling from the sky = great visual.<br />* I really, really liked some of Theia's friends--and they were proof that the author could write snappy and unstilted dialogue. Her best friend Donny is hilarious, and I liked Amelia, Gabriel, Mike, etc. as well. All the early interactions between the friends felt very grounded and real, although the roles they play towards the end of the book are less convincing. <br />* Some of the self-deprecating humor took me by surprise. Even while I was rolling my eyes at all the melodramatic stuff that drags on through the first part of the book, I kept going because every once in awhile the author would pop out a surprisingly funny remark that poked fun at what was going on. More of that tone would definitely have improved the book, however.<br /><br /><b>What really made the book enjoyable to me, though:</b><br /><br />* A fantastic villain! When she shows up about two-thirds of the way through, I sat up and paid attention. Her physical being, her arch dialogue, and her evil scheming were all really well done. I wasn't entirely convinced by the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[disguise she takes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> later on in the book, but I still really liked seeing her.<br />* A big, big sacrifice that is made that I thought was extraordinarily well done. Based on what had come before, I wasn't expecting it to be that emotionally compelling.<br />* The turn of tables (related to the sacrifice) and shift in POV was pretty interesting.<br />* I ended up liking the new and changed Theia quite a lot. <i>There's</i> the backbone we were all waiting for! It's a shame it didn't happen sooner in the storyline.<br />* I love love loved the creepy evil minions. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Skeletons. Women stitched together with black thread and wobbly heads. Who violently BATHE her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Awesome! Would love to have seen more done with them. <br /><br />I'm torn between how I felt at the beginning of the book (bored, somewhat annoyed) and the end of the book (really excited and interested), so I'm not really sure whether it's something I'd recommend. I'd say that if you're intrigued by the premise, it's worth a read just so long as you keep your expectations in check. I, for one, will definitely be checking out the next book to see what the new and improved Theia will do.<br /><br /><i>This review may also be found at <a>The Midnight Garden</a></i>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="766260603515273826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_132965064" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132965064" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132965064?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132965064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer513724715797136182"><i>Dear YA,<br/><br/>1. Please don’t let this be another book on star crossed lovers whose relationship is doomed from the beginning because one is in danger of being killed by the other.<br/>2. Please, please, please no more love triangles!<br/>3. Please make the heroine a heroine by which, I mean a thinking, independent, strong-willed and <b>self-aware</b> young woman… who could be construed as a positive role model for your target audience. And let the male lead be more than just her love interest. Let him have a more int</i></span>
  <span id="freeText513724715797136182" style="display:none"><i>Dear YA,<br /><br />1. Please don’t let this be another book on star crossed lovers whose relationship is doomed from the beginning because one is in danger of being killed by the other.<br />2. Please, please, please no more love triangles!<br />3. Please make the heroine a heroine by which, I mean a thinking, independent, strong-willed and <b>self-aware</b> young woman… who could be construed as a positive role model for your target audience. And let the male lead be more than just her love interest. Let him have a more interesting role and not just eye candy. <br />4. Please don’t let the dialogue be riddled with “now-isms.” <br /><br />Sincerely,<br />Isa</i><br /><br />****<br /><br />First off, I will restrain myself from making <s>sparkly</s> comparisons because while there are similarities, there are enough positive elements to balance the book out. Now, color me surprised: I actually enjoyed this one! Among the positives that FALLING UNDER has to offer are the dialogue, the shifting mood and the dream sequences. <br /><br />But first, to the negatives. (I tried to keep myself from making comparisons, but sometimes it just cannot be helped.) Theia is virginal, cosseted, and a little priggish. Her being virginal, and cosseted led me to the question of why. Her father’s treatment of her left me befuddled. It begged the question(s) A. What’s wrong with her? Was she another one of those girls ala A Walk to Remember heroine… goody-goody and sheltered. (B) Or had she been not so goody-goody prior to the books opening; thus, requiring an iron fist in her upbringing (C.) Or had there been a tragedy that just pushed him to act the way he was acting… or (D.) Was it an English stodgy thing? As I was saying, she’s pretty tame. I would not have minded that particular fact, but she’s tame <b>AND</b> then oblivious to why the male lead was <i>obsessing </i> over her. <br /><br />Add to that a giggly moment (whether done by design or the product of my gutter brain, you’ll just have to judge) of when she actually says, <b>“Take me.”</b> I don’t know, but bodice-ripping-Regency/Harlequin-esque historical-romance much? This mental image might have been compounded by the old sound of Theia’s thoughts. As said, she is virginal and cosseted. And apparently very prim and proper, in her thoughts as well. She just sounded old (more on this later.) <br /><br />Throw in a mercurial Haden. Flirt one moment ass hole the next. I do not see the charm of one so fickle. Would you go after a guy who would leave you whilst a storm is going on. I am sounding positively old fashioned, but the guy just showed his true colors at that moment in the book. <br /><br />All that said, this book wasn’t bad. In fact I found myself satisfied by the turn of events. Yes, it was a little too pat… but still consider: <br /><br />I really enjoyed the darker feel to it. Moments of Falling Under are a horror/slasher film montage. Burning man, Night terrors. Mysterious stranger. Gothick-y music possibly leading to her (a) death or (b) love. Sewn lips, Chopped up brides. <br /><br />Then there were all the dream sequences that reminded me of Beetlejuice and Chicken Run. I have a deep seated fear of clay-mation. This probably stems from a childhood scare-fest involving dolls coming alive and hacking away at limbs carelessly strewn willy-nilly over the bed’s edge… wait, what was I saying? The dreams sequences caught my attention because they had the same feel as Corpse Bride etc. (*shudder*) It was this that, I can honestly, kept me reading… despite Haden’s hot and cold attitude toward her…despite Theia’s virginal and innocent disposition…despite her father’s tendency toward being overbearing.<br /><br />The language attracted me too. I have said that her thoughts sounded old, much older than her purported seventeen years. Despite this incongruence, I went with it. As a result I felt as she felt. Her confusion was mine; as was her frustration. That’s where the authenticity ended for me though because once her conscious interactions began, she started sounding typical YA heroine. (Daughter who had not rebelled but wants to. Friend in the middle… neither super pretty nor super smart… but wealthy enough. AND thankfully she didn’t always speak so “old” just serious at times.)<br /><br />The most authentic lines sprang from Donny’s lips. I liked her particularly since she had a tendency towards being brazen. I liked that she spoke her mind in a very “current” way, but managed not to bludgeon said current-ness to death (as has happened in some books.) <br /><br />And speaking of Donny, I liked the friendship dynamic going on in this one. They are a study in contrast I suppose. Especially, with Donny the brazen one, Amelia the outgoing sweet one and Theia, the heroine the socially awkward one (Hmmm… this assessment might actually be more apt under the “Argh” column). Put them together and you could end up with a whole girl.<br /><br />So in response. <br /><br />Yes, it does start with an “I love you, but I might kill you, so let’s just not,” BUT I got a kick out of how the author addressed that problem <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[By using the problem twice. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />And, Allelujah! There is no love triangle! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ unless you count the fact that Haden is half human and half demon, in which case is there a triangle? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Sadly, the heroine is a cardboard cut out of YA heroines: meek and oblivious to her charms… AND, Yes, the male lead does start out as mere fuel for her dreams. BUT I do love how the author turned them on their heads in the latter half of the book. <br /><br />The dialogue while current was not over done.<br /><br />So over all: Read it! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="513724715797136182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129830519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129830519" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320017147p2/4515165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129830519?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=that-made-no-sense">that-made-no-sense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=goodreads-first-reads">goodreads-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129830519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17299515868274498477">I was so excited to read Falling Under after I won a copy on Goodreads First Reads. The concept of meeting a mysterious, "devastatingly handsome" guy from your dreams sounded captivating, but Falling Under was too much of the worn-thin "I'm a jerk to you but you love me anyway" romance, and the parts that were original were too dark for me. I'd recommend Falling Under to those that love the darker side of paranormal fiction (not me).<br/><br/>Theia, Theia, Theia. The author tells us things about her, but </span>
  <span id="freeText17299515868274498477" style="display:none">I was so excited to read Falling Under after I won a copy on Goodreads First Reads. The concept of meeting a mysterious, "devastatingly handsome" guy from your dreams sounded captivating, but Falling Under was too much of the worn-thin "I'm a jerk to you but you love me anyway" romance, and the parts that were original were too dark for me. I'd recommend Falling Under to those that love the darker side of paranormal fiction (not me).<br /><br />Theia, Theia, Theia. The author tells us things about her, but Theia's actions show us a completely different story. She puts herself in danger. Again. And again. She's supposed to be this incredible musician and smart and rational, but she makes so many TSTL choices that I gave up. Haden even tells her why he's there--and it involves Theia in a horrible way--and yet she still comes back for more. WHY??? Why can't we ever get a heroine who tells these kinds of guys where they can go? Read the back cover--Theia doesn't want to resist Haden, even if it costs her her soul. Ugh.<br /><br />And Haden? My tolerance of the "I'm hot so you love me even though I'm a jerk and treat you abysmally" guy must be all used up. (Again, this theme in young adult fiction is getting REALLY old.) The whole "hot/cold" guy thing has been done before and done a lot better. Haden became more tolerable as the book went on, but I wanted to infuse some rationality into Theia for 3/4 of the book for making STUPID, STUPID choices involving Haden. Why couldn't Theia go for a charismatic, thoughtful guy like Gabe?<br /><br />Falling Under is dark. It has the TSTL heroine, the jerk bad boy, and the idiot parent that we see in so many books these days. It wasn't for me, but if you like dark paranormal fiction with a smattering of Twilight, you may like it.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17299515868274498477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_102546385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102546385" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102546385?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102546385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9044398739949159727">This book was totally not what I was expecting. Definitely a lot more dark and wickedly twisted than I ever would have expected, yet I think that is why I liked it to much. Under was a complete creep-fest.... faceless beings, skeletons.... stitched together people.... rivers of tears. I had those huge eyes.... O_O .... and the expression of "no f-ing way!" it was awesome.<br/><br/>The characters in this novel were extremely well written. Everyone of them had truly unique qualities that made them very hard</span>
  <span id="freeText9044398739949159727" style="display:none">This book was totally not what I was expecting. Definitely a lot more dark and wickedly twisted than I ever would have expected, yet I think that is why I liked it to much. Under was a complete creep-fest.... faceless beings, skeletons.... stitched together people.... rivers of tears. I had those huge eyes.... O_O .... and the expression of "no f-ing way!" it was awesome.<br /><br />The characters in this novel were extremely well written. Everyone of them had truly unique qualities that made them very hard to forget. Theia's friends Donny and Amelia aka Ame (how to you say that anyway... like "Amy" or "Aim"?) couldn't have been more different not only from each other but from Theia as well, and for some reason that worked incredibly well. Donny, what can I say about her, she is hilarious! Those girls were some good friends! I want me some friends like Donny and Ame! And I also loved Varnie! If you read this novel for one reason, read it for Varnie!<br /><br />I'm not going to lie.... Haden and Theia.... the whole "stay away from me, I'm dangerous" I thought, oh please not this again... and I can honestly say, it's not like that again. There was a little insta-romance, Theia falls for Haden hard and fast, even though the guy is jerk. Yet, I loved how that gave Theia this whole other personality. She was assertive and sure-footed when it came to Haden, I liked her much better that way. So somehow the insta-romance worked for me. I mean it's not like she hadn't already met the guy in her dreams! I felt like they already had a "relationship" before they started interacting in-real-life.<br /><br />The plot while a little slow in the beginning, will slap you in the face when you least expect it. I had that huge eye thing going on again.... O_O... yeah just like that.<br /><br />An excellent debut! Didn't realize this one was going to be a series, but I am certainly looking forward to the next installment. This is one wickedly twisted love story!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9044398739949159727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119480227" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4176166-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600307841p2/4176166.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119480227?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/4176166-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9583442-falling-under">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=atlp-review">atlp-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4176166-cindy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119480227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15873609879404519968"><b>This review may also be found on <a><i>A Thousand Little Pages</i></a>.</b><br/><br/>2.5/5<br/><br/>A shy girl living a seemingly normal life? Check.<br/>A hot and mysterious guy appearing out of nowhere? Check.<br/>Instant, unexplainable, and inevitable attraction blossoming as the two gaze at each other fatefully through a pane of glass? Check.<br/><br/>Haden/Mr. Dangerous-and-Brooding: <i>Stay away from me, lamb.* I’m dangerous.</i><br/>Theia/Ms. Radiant-Sunshine: <i>But I don’t want to. I think I’m in love with you!</i><br/>Check.<br/><br/>Does this sound just a teensy bit familiar</span>
  <span id="freeText15873609879404519968" style="display:none"><b>This review may also be found on <a><i>A Thousand Little Pages</i></a>.</b><br /><br />2.5/5<br /><br />A shy girl living a seemingly normal life? Check.<br />A hot and mysterious guy appearing out of nowhere? Check.<br />Instant, unexplainable, and inevitable attraction blossoming as the two gaze at each other fatefully through a pane of glass? Check.<br /><br />Haden/Mr. Dangerous-and-Brooding: <i>Stay away from me, lamb.* I’m dangerous.</i><br />Theia/Ms. Radiant-Sunshine: <i>But I don’t want to. I think I’m in love with you!</i><br />Check.<br /><br />Does this sound just a teensy bit familiar yet…? Ugh, the first two-thirds of the book was a complete rehash of <i>Twilight</i>, albeit a better-written one. A solid 2 stars -- not horrible, and yet not horribly original. I had to roll my eyes a few times here and there. A couple of facepalms appeared, too.<br /><br />What bumped the rating up to 2.5 stars was the last third of <i>Falling Under</i>. Told in the perspective of Haden instead of Theia, this portion of the book, titled <i>Up is Down</i>, is infinitely more interesting plot-wise and such a joy to read after the cough<i>Twilight</i>cough review we got before. If only the entire book was like the last part. Alas, it was not to be.<br /><br />Overall, this book is worth it if you’re willing to wade through some clichés and overdone plot lines first. <i>Falling Under</i>’s invigorating ending certainly left me in need of the sequel.<br /><br />*Seriously? Haden has to refer to Theia as his <i>lamb</i>, too? Please… -.-<br /><br />Book Source: Borrowed</span>

<div id="review_122050141" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122050141" />
    <a title="Katie(babs)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs"><img alt="Katie(babs)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242522005p2/179852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122050141?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie(babs)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie(babs)" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs">Katie(babs)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122050141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9267014580990746594">I’m a sucker for a sexy cover. Gwen Hayes has such a cover for her debut, Falling Under, a supernatural YA about a young girl, who dreams of a dark world and of the boy who resides there, who in turns enters her world and tries to claim her soul. I had some reservations about this book because of my recent dismay over the large amount of YA Paranormal books published that are trying to ride the Twilight train for all it’s worth. Time and again I’m seeing a lonely female protagonist with MIA pare</span>
  <span id="freeText9267014580990746594" style="display:none">I’m a sucker for a sexy cover. Gwen Hayes has such a cover for her debut, Falling Under, a supernatural YA about a young girl, who dreams of a dark world and of the boy who resides there, who in turns enters her world and tries to claim her soul. I had some reservations about this book because of my recent dismay over the large amount of YA Paranormal books published that are trying to ride the Twilight train for all it’s worth. Time and again I’m seeing a lonely female protagonist with MIA parental figures and the darkly, seductive boy who enters the picture suddenly, and with one look or touch, they decide they’re each other’s soul mates even before the heroine is old enough to vote.<br /><br />There are a few of these tropes found in Falling Under and 30 pages in I had some concerns. But Gwen’s writing really shines. It’s superbly written. She doesn’t talk down to her audience and brings forth topics such as suppressed teens and their desire for sex that comes out with a vengeance. If Falling Under was a candy bar, it would be Hershey’s dark chocolate.<br /><br />The first line grabs you- “Everything changed the night I saw the burning man fall from the sky”. The heroine, Theia Alderson witnesses this outside her bedroom window as she plays with her new iPhone her rigid and cold British father has given to her as a gift. Theia feels she’s stuck in a gilded cage since her father expects her to remain in control at all times and act accordingly as he sees fit. Theia spends her days playing violin and longing for her mother who died after giving birth to her. Theia has the urge to be reckless and carefree like her mother was, but her father squashes her rebellion. That is until the shock of burning man falling from the sky and her dreams of a far off distant place where she meets a man-boy who makes her feel all tingly inside. <br /><br />Theia may be somewhat of an outcast at school, but her two good friends- Donny and Amelia are there for her. They want her to rebel and do something as shocking as go to a dance club with them. Theia longs to live on the edge but doesn’t want to rock the boat. Things become exciting when a new student arrives at the school. His name is Haden Black and he’s the boy from her dreams. The moment her eyes meet his, she knows her life will never be the same again. Haden flirts with Theia as if he’s interested in her, but then backs away and cruelly taunts her by being touchy feely with other girls. Theia cannot understand what’s going on and why Haden one minute acts as her friend, but then pushes her away. He says he can’t give her what she wants. But Theia continues to dream of Haden, where she longs to stay in this world, otherwise known as the Under realm where Haden’s demon mother is the queen and wants Theia to be Haden’s bride in order for her to give him a child she can mold into her own evil ways. <br /><br />Falling Under is very seductive reading. A few of the YA Paranormal authors should take note because this is how a YA Paranormal should be written. Yes, Theia is oh so innocent, reserved and has emotional issues, and yes Haden is dark, mysterious and has touch of evil inside of him, but these two connect on such a level where it’s not cheesy. Gwen puts a nice little spin on their relationship is more adult in nature. There’s a great deal of sexual tension on the pages that is borderline erotic in the teen sense. I also loved how Gwen showed that even though Theia may be at odds with her distant father, she has a great support with her two girlfriends and the boys they become interested in, who in turn help Theia out. Their dialogue and interactions don’t feel contrived and really flow well.<br /><br />Falling Under has a feeling of two movies while I read with Labyrinth and Legend. Haden reminds me of David Bowie’s character, Jareth.<br /><br />I’ve been going back and forth on my grade for Falling Under. At times I felt the explanation for things were lacking, such as Haden living in a very expensive hotel and not even the school administration asking for proof of his parents. Also, we’re given reasons why Haden wants to be with Theia in her realm, but there’s no talk about why she suddenly dreams of him and how he came to invade them. Also the ending seems a bit rushed. These small issues may take away some enjoyment for readers, but again, Gwen makes up for it with her fabulous writing. With that in mind, I’m giving Falling Under a B+ because this is one YA book that really kept me riveted and interested in seeing if Haden and Theia will have their HEA.<br /><br />Gwen Hayes is a much welcomed addition to the YA genre and one I’m going to keep my eye on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9267014580990746594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_147364097" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147364097" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285872916p2/2276205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147364097?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147364097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1186172997963603243">Hi, my name is Kelly, and I’m addicted to underworlds.<br/><br/>And it’s the fantastic realm of “Under” that, for me, was the best part of <i>Falling Under</i>. Gwen Hayes uses several tropes that have become overused in YA paranormal romance, but the book is better written than many of its peers, and Hayes’ creativity bursts out of the bounds of the formula every time she shows us a scene from Under.<br/><br/>At first, this feels like a lot of books we’ve read before. Reserved, virginal Theia meets a mysterious boy, Hade</span>
  <span id="freeText1186172997963603243" style="display:none">Hi, my name is Kelly, and I’m addicted to underworlds.<br /><br />And it’s the fantastic realm of “Under” that, for me, was the best part of <i>Falling Under</i>. Gwen Hayes uses several tropes that have become overused in YA paranormal romance, but the book is better written than many of its peers, and Hayes’ creativity bursts out of the bounds of the formula every time she shows us a scene from Under.<br /><br />At first, this feels like a lot of books we’ve read before. Reserved, virginal Theia meets a mysterious boy, Haden, at her high school. They’re assigned to work as partners in class. Haden tries to protect Theia from his dark secret, alternating between treating her coldly and being a control freak. When, finally, he withdraws from her life in a last-ditch effort to save her, Theia resorts to self-destructive measures to see him again. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Sleeping pills, in a scene that chilled me more than any underworld beastie in the book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />An additional issue is Theia’s father who, we are told, is stiflingly overprotective. Many YA characters have neglectful parents who conveniently evaporate so their kids can have their adventures unimpeded. Having an overprotective parent struck me as a refreshing change, not to mention more relatable for me based on my own personal experience! I thought the dream sequences — more about those later — were a clever way for Hayes to give Theia adventures even though she was restricted in the real world. Unfortunately, though, Theia’s father does vanish for much of the book and seems more akin to the usual absent parents than he’s meant to be. I know about overprotective fathers, and it doesn’t seem realistic that he would go on a business trip and leave her in the house alone. He’d take her along, or else bring in Auntie Horrible to babysit. <br /><br />But when I was frustrated with the first half of <i>Falling Under</i>, the dream sequences kept me reading. Theia visits a strange place in her dreams, one that’s both beautiful and nightmarish, and where her relationship with Haden is rather different from the one that exists in the waking world. Later, when Theia is taken bodily into Under, it makes for terrific reading. It’s as if Twilight suddenly turned into Pan’s Labyrinth. Creepy, yet filled with strange beauty, Under is incredibly compelling.<br /><br />The other great part about <i>Falling Under</i> is the friendships. The bond between Theia and her quirky friends, which later includes several endearing guys as well, is wonderful. Nowhere is this more evident than in the most un-clichéd prom scene I’ve read in YA literature. I don’t want to spoil it for you, but what happens is way more interesting than the stereotypical scene where it’s an enchanted evening and the protagonists get to feel like princes and princesses for a few hours. (And really, how many of us really had proms that lived up to that fantasy anyway?)<br /><br />I also liked seeing Theia finally develop a backbone, though it’s a little bothersome that it only happens when a guy enters her life. I can deal with that, though, since one of the people she learns to stand up to is Haden himself.<br /><br />The latter half of <i>Falling Under</i> is enjoyable enough that I very nearly gave the book a fourth star — but in the end decided I was too disturbed by the scene mentioned above in spoiler text; I felt it was romanticized too much. I do look forward to reading more of Gwen Hayes’s books in the future, and can’t wait to see more of Under. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1186172997963603243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115234651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115234651" />
    <a title="Diana~ (Kiss Me Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3809774-diana-kiss-me-books"><img alt="Diana~ (Kiss Me Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603607690p2/3809774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115234651?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana~ (Kiss Me Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana~ (Kiss Me Books)" href="/user/show/3809774-diana-kiss-me-books">Diana~ (Kiss Me Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809774-diana-kiss-me-books?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809774-diana-kiss-me-books?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3809774-diana-kiss-me-books?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115234651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9948158686653479401">For <b>Gwen Hayes</b>'s first debut, this book was pretty amazing. The flow of the story, the intricate characters and the writing that the author creates was just mesmorizing. I can't stop thinking about it! Plus, I'm also a sucker for tortured heroes... and Haden Black is that one. I didn't think I would have shed so many tears for these two people who, even though they loved each other, could not be together. <b>Falling Under</b> is a story about finding the love of your life and fighting for what you beli</span>
  <span id="freeText9948158686653479401" style="display:none">For <b>Gwen Hayes</b>'s first debut, this book was pretty amazing. The flow of the story, the intricate characters and the writing that the author creates was just mesmorizing. I can't stop thinking about it! Plus, I'm also a sucker for tortured heroes... and Haden Black is that one. I didn't think I would have shed so many tears for these two people who, even though they loved each other, could not be together. <b>Falling Under</b> is a story about finding the love of your life and fighting for what you believe in, as well as the confounding emotion of wanting someone so much that you might end up hurting them. It was beautifully written and I'm <i>dying</i> to read the second installment of this series! If you're into dark paranormal romance with plenty of sexual undertones everywhere, then this is the book for you. I mean holy cow, Haden is one sexy and emotional hero who loves deeply and pretty much <i>
  <b>darkly</b>
</i>.<br /><br />My favorite quote from Haden was this: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <blockquote>
    <i>“Darkness lives in me, Theia. Inside of me. Like a sickness. And right next to it, intertwined with it, are my feelings for you. If I act on one, I’ll act on the other. The darkness in me wants you the way a black hole eats stars. I dream of tasting you, devouring you.” His eyes darkened terribly. <br /><br />This isn’t a crush; it’s an obsession. You are never not in my thoughts. Your scent carries across a room and paralyzes me with longing. I don’t want to hold your hand. Part of me wants to set you on fire and hold you while the flame consumes us both, to eat your heart so I know that only I possess it entirely. Are you scared now? Does your human mind comprehend the danger at last? I’m not like you. I’m not human, not completely anyway.”</i>
  </blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There were times when I wanted to smack Theia because she was one of those heroines... that needed 'saving.' She was characterized as an obedient daughter who wanted to break out of her shell, but never actually could or wanted to. It went on for awhile until one day, everything changed. I have to admit, the author created a pretty unique story in which the world in which Haden lived in was just so dark and beautiful.<br /><br />Haden claims that he is evil and in a sense, that is true. He is part of something that will irrevocably change Theia's life forever and I think that is what makes this book so damn <i>mind blowing</i>! The ending was especially that because of the sudden twist in the story as well as the change in the POV. I never would have thought that the author would switch up the story like that. Either way, this was a wonderful story that definitely deserves attention! THIS, is how a YA Paranormal story should be written.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9948158686653479401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_101394679" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101394679" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393730599p2/1894085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101394679?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/1894085-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1894085-alexa?shelf=tour">tour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101394679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15336730160966535460"><br/>My review can also be found on my blog <a href='http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2011/02/review-falling-under-by-gwen-hayes.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Collections</a>.<br/><br/>It all starts when Theia sees a burning man fall from the sky. After that she begins having strange and creepy dreams about a boy she's never seen before. Things become even weirder when she finds out he's the newest student in school. For some reason, he acts cold towards her, treating her the opposite of how he does in her dreams. She can't figure him out, and although she knows there's something not quite right about him, she can't stop herse</span>
  <span id="freeText15336730160966535460" style="display:none"><br />My review can also be found on my blog <a href="http://collections-books.blogspot.com/2011/02/review-falling-under-by-gwen-hayes.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Collections</a>.<br /><br />It all starts when Theia sees a burning man fall from the sky. After that she begins having strange and creepy dreams about a boy she's never seen before. Things become even weirder when she finds out he's the newest student in school. For some reason, he acts cold towards her, treating her the opposite of how he does in her dreams. She can't figure him out, and although she knows there's something not quite right about him, she can't stop herself from getting close to him. <br /><br />I thought the first half of <i>Falling Under</i> was similar to what is seen in a lot of YA paranormals. There's the underconfident girl (Theia), who is drawn to the new, mysterious boy (Haden) at school. And even though the new boy seems to be interested in her as well, he's not exactly nice to her and tells her to stay away. But she can't and neither can he. Sound familiar? Well, I think that's why it was a bit of a struggle for me getting through the beginning of the book. <br /><br />While the first half didn't stand out to me, I thought the last half of the story made up for it. Things started getting interesting the moment Haden revealed what he was and his purpose for being there. I don't believe I've read a YA paranormal with that type of paranormal creature. It explained why Haden treated Theia the way he did. The last part of the book wasn't quite perfect though. The entire book was a bit fast paced, and I was fine with that, but I would have liked to learn more about Haden's world near the end. Overall, I liked what we did get. <br /><br />After finishing the book, there were some things I was left wondering about like <i>Why was Theia immune to Haden's Lure?</i> and <i>How do Theia and Haden adjust?</i> If there's a sequel, which I really hope there is, I will definitely check it out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15336730160966535460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1342860750" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10927025436656290604">Okay where do I even begin with this book?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635219ra/15605350.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Our “heroine” turns out to be seriously dull. She was just, the most boring main character I have ever read about... and I’ve read <i>Hush Hush</i> so that says something. Ugh, and I knew it from the start too, when she is laying on her bed pensively reading her book in her nightgown thinking really deep thoughts. You’re 17! Go out with friends! Read a magazine! Do something <i>slightly</i> interesting! I guess I’m not one to talk, because I’m 17 and I love reading, </span>
  <span id="freeText10927025436656290604" style="display:none">Okay where do I even begin with this book?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635219ra/15605350.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Our “heroine” turns out to be seriously dull. She was just, the most boring main character I have ever read about... and I’ve read <i>Hush Hush</i> so that says something. Ugh, and I knew it from the start too, when she is laying on her bed pensively reading her book in her nightgown thinking really deep thoughts. You’re 17! Go out with friends! Read a magazine! Do something <i>slightly</i> interesting! I guess I’m not one to talk, because I’m 17 and I love reading, but she makes it sound like she’s reading Shakespeare while listening to Mozart.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635219ra/15605351.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But don’t worry, after this you will definitely be entertained by this book, not because it’s genuinely a funny book, but because it is so ridiculous. I laughed SO FREAKING HARD when Theia and Haden first meet. So while the virginal princess is sitting in her room listening to Beethoven or some shit, she looks out her window and sees Haden falling from the sky <i>on fire</i>. While he is falling out of the sky like a meteor, Theia isn’t shocked by the falling aspect, or the fire aspect, no… she discerns something strange about his <i>eyes</i>. Yes, because his eyes are the only weird thing in that situation.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635219ra/15605352.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But that’s not even the best part. When she goes outside to try to help Haden, he looks at her, and with his dying breath he says “worth…the…fall”. BAHAHAHAAHA yeah, because apparently being set on fire and falling god knows how far to the ground, was all worth it just to see her face. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635219ra/15605353.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And do you know why Hayden was apparently so in love with Theia in the first place? Because he saw her playing the <i>violin</i>. Right, because that’s what guys are really after… your <i>violin skills</i>. Protect your instruments girls, from the predators of the world. I mean when my mom told me that guys are only after one thing, I had no idea she was talking about <i>musical talent</i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635219ra/15605354.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Okay I have been mocking this book mercilessly without even telling you exactly why I hated it so much. Honestly, I absolutely abhor the characters. That’s right, abhor. I’ve already told you why I dislike Theia. She’s boring, sheltered, boring, helpless, and just so god-damn boringggggggg! But I’ll tell you why I hate Haden so much. First of all, he’s a hell demon and he acts like it. Second of all, he just says the creepiest things. At one point he says something about wanting to eat Theia's heart or something so that he knows it always belongs to him...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635995ra/15605491.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Third, there was this scene where he <s>dances with</s> dry humps this other girl while making purposeful eye contact with Theia, because he knows that Theia can feel it with some kind of weird-ass demon connection. Ew. Just, ew.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635219ra/15605356.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I guess all I’m trying to say is if you like good books… don’t read this.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437635219ra/15605357.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Check out the rest of my reviews on my blog <a href="https://readallnightsleepallday.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Read All Night, Sleep All Day</a></span>

This is a wonderful and different paranormal that involves no Vampires or Werewolves, nor any Angels or Fairies!<br/><br/>It's about Theia, a very withdrawn and sheltered young girl who lives with her extremely overprotective and strict father.<br/><br/>When a burning man falls from the sky, everything starts to change. <br/><br/>When the totally hot new guy, Haden Black, starts school, Theia is drawn to him and she c</span>
  <span id="freeText3756577496687602544" style="display:none">First of all thank you to Goodreads! I won an ARC of this book through their first reads program!<br /><br />I loved it! This is a wonderful and different paranormal that involves no Vampires or Werewolves, nor any Angels or Fairies!<br /><br />It's about Theia, a very withdrawn and sheltered young girl who lives with her extremely overprotective and strict father.<br /><br />When a burning man falls from the sky, everything starts to change. <br /><br />When the totally hot new guy, Haden Black, starts school, Theia is drawn to him and she can't figure out why he seems so familiar... <br /><br />...he's the one from her dreams..!<br /><br />The writing is beautiful and the chemistry between Haden and Theia captivating! I also really like all of the secondary characters..<br /><br />I'm really hoping for a sequel to this one!</span>

<div id="review_168090916" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168090916" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_126852280" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126852280" />
    <a title="Shawna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4179527-shawna"><img alt="Shawna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339787817p2/4179527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126852280?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawna" href="/user/show/4179527-shawna">Shawna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA Paranormal Fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4179527-shawna?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4179527-shawna?shelf=ya-paranormal-or-paranormal-roma">ya-paranormal-or-paranormal-roma</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126852280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13581118377738402149">First I must say thank you to the GoodReads First Reads program for the ARC!!!! I won a copy through the Goodreads giveaway!!<br/><br/>Falling Under was a very unique story and not the usual YA Paranormal books. No Vampires, No Werewolves, and No Fairies, oh my. It was so well written and Gwen Hayes did a fantastic job at describing things that it was so easy to picture. There were some parts of the book that were a little slow but definitely nothing that made me put the book down.<br/><br/>Theia can't help feel th</span>
  <span id="freeText13581118377738402149" style="display:none">First I must say thank you to the GoodReads First Reads program for the ARC!!!! I won a copy through the Goodreads giveaway!!<br /><br />Falling Under was a very unique story and not the usual YA Paranormal books. No Vampires, No Werewolves, and No Fairies, oh my. It was so well written and Gwen Hayes did a fantastic job at describing things that it was so easy to picture. There were some parts of the book that were a little slow but definitely nothing that made me put the book down.<br /><br />Theia can't help feel this draw she has for the new boy Haden, whom she dreamt about before his arrival at school. The pull is so strong she dreams of him every night. She feels the need to be near him and feels when he is around before she can even see him. All Thiea wants is to be with Haden but yet Haden as his own agenda.<br /><br />As Haden begins to get his plan in motion, he also starts to fall for Theia. One minute he has to be near her, the next he is teasing her and shutting her out. Theia doesn't seemed fazed at all by any of Haden's games or words. She knows deep down that Haden feels it too and she sets out to conquer him. Grant it Haden can be a jerk to her but you soon find out that there is a good reason for her to stay away from him.<br /><br />With her best friends Ameila (a natural raw talent of physic abilities) and Donny (the over protective non-believer hard core realist) they soon discover there is more to Haden than meets the eye. Her best friends will do whatever is necessary to save Theia in the end. We only hope it will be enough.<br /><br />I must say Gabe was definately a good character. I loved how he was able to break through Donny's (Donetella's) walls and her rough exterior to appreciate her for what she truly is. A person that will do anything for her friends. Varnie, what's not to like about Varnie. I only hope that Amelia will start to see him the way he sees her, rather than her obsession with Mike who is definitley a few bricks short of a load. <br /><br />I definitely thought I had the book figured out and new how the book would end. Well, I was wrong and the way it ended was a huge shocker for me. I did not see it coming at all and that is what I loved the most. I am assuming with the way Falling Under ended there is going to be a sequel. At least I hope there is a sequel. One that I can't wait to read. I look forward taking the ride with the characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13581118377738402149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
